  > 3. Error logs appear in: ts-delivery-service (48 errors), ts-food-service (56 errors), ts-notification-service (48 errors), ts-order-service (1 error), ts-preserve-service (1 error)
  > 
  > The preserve endpoint trace path seems to be:
  > - loadgenerator → ts-ui-dashboard → ts-preserve-service → [various downstream services]
  > 
  > The high avg_duration of ~20 seconds in the loadgenerator span is suspicious. The ts-ui-dashboard span shows avg ~17.8 seconds. The ts-preserve-service span shows only ~3.2 seconds avg, but that's only 3 spans vs 23 for the ui-dashboard and 20 for loadgenerator.
  > 
  > Wait - the loadgenerator has 20 spans with status "Error" and avg 20s duration. The ts-ui-dashboard has 23 spans with 200 response. The ts-preserve-service has only 3 spans.
  > 
  > This is very interesting. It looks like:
  > - Most requests from loadgenerator to preserve endpoint timed out (20 seconds, status Error)
  > - Only 3 requests actually made it through to ts-preserve-service
  > - The ts-ui-dashboard processed 23 requests (3 got 200, but perhaps 20 timed out or hung waiting for something)

  > 
  > Actually wait - the loadgenerator shows 20 Error spans and 3 Ok spans. The ts-ui-dashboard shows 23 spans with http 200. This is curious because the loadgenerator says Error but dashboard says 200.

  > 1. The trace details for the preserve endpoint - especially the calls from ts-preserve-service to downstream services

  >

  > 1. Security check → ts-security-service
  > 2. Assurance check → ts-assurance-service

  > 4. Contacts → ts-contacts-service
  > 5. Travel information → ts-travel-service or ts-travel2-service
  > 6. Order creation → ts-order-service
  >

  > - ts-train-food-service (for train food)

  > Looking at the normal trace spans from ts-preserve-service:
  > 1. GET (23ms) → security
  > 2. GET (13ms) → contacts
  > 3. POST (850ms) → travel (span c0313fd7711af0a0)
  > 4. POST (31ms) → food order (span ed40b94f3542ebb3)
  > 5. POST (12ms) → something (span db6aa724ee811e58)

  > 9. GET (6ms) → something (span e0610d2a65f5fff5)
  > 
  > Each of these is a SEPARATE span from ts-preserve-service's PreserveController.preserve!
  > 
  > So for the ABNORMAL trace "7a2c8b3c...", the ts-preserve-service should have multiple POST spans (one per downstream call). But we only see:
  > 1. GET (security)
  > 2. GET (contacts)
  > 3. POST (6.41 seconds) - this is the ONE POST span
  > 
  > This means:
  > - The travel service call (54ms) IS inside the POST (6.41s) span
  > - But what comes AFTER the travel service? The span "eda961ae..." (6.41s) contains the entire remaining 6.35 seconds
  > 
  > In the normal trace, after the travel service, there would be a SEPARATE POST span for the next downstream service. But in the abnormal trace, there's only ONE POST span and it lasts 6.41 seconds.
  > 
  > This is the KEY: In the normal flow, ts-preserve-service's "PreserveController.preserve" calls:
  > 1. GET → security
  > 2. GET → contacts

  > - ts-preserve-service is doing something synchronously inside this method after the travel service returns
  > - The span represents a method that calls travel service AND then something else that's hanging
  > 
  > OR: The POST spans in normal are all SEPARATE steps, and in abnormal, they've been collapsed or the second POST span (food service call) is taking 6.35 seconds.
  > 
  > Actually, I think I've been overanalyzing this. Let me focus on what we KNOW:
  > 
  > 1. In normal trace, ts-preserve-service calls multiple services sequentially
  > 2. In abnormal trace "7a2c8b3c...", after the contacts check, there's only ONE POST span from ts-preserve-service (6.41 seconds) containing the travel service (54ms)
  > 3. The remaining 6.35 seconds in that POST span is UNACCOUNTED FOR
  > 4. No other spans from ts-preserve-service appear after this
  > 
  > The most likely explanation:
  > - The ts-preserve-service POST span (6.41s) is actually the TRAVEL SERVICE CALL span
  > - After travel service responds (04:07:35.954), ts-preserve-service immediately tries to call the NEXT service (food or order service)
  > - This NEXT service call hangs for 6.35 seconds
  > - But since the method is synchronous and the span is still "open", the hanging call appears within the same span context
  > - However, the hanging call NEVER GENERATES A CHILD SPAN because the downstream service is unresponsive
  > 
  > This pattern is exactly what happens when a service makes a synchronous HTTP call to a COMPLETELY UNAVAILABLE service:
  > - The caller's span stays open (waiting for the response)
  > - The callee doesn't generate any spans (because it's dead/unreachable)
  > - After the HTTP timeout (6+ seconds), the caller gives up
  > 
  > So the root question is: WHICH service is ts-preserve-service calling after the travel service that takes 6+ seconds?
  > 
  > Based on the normal trace order: POST (850ms) → ts-travel-service, then POST (31ms) → ts-food-service orders. 
  >

  > - span c0313fd7711af0a0: POST (850ms) - child of PreserveController.preserve
  > - span ed40b94f3542ebb3: POST (31ms) - child of PreserveController.preserve
  > - span db6aa724ee811e58: POST (12ms) - child of PreserveController.preserve
  > 
  > These are ALL separate POST spans! In the NORMAL trace, there are multiple POST spans each going to different services.
  > 
  > In the ABNORMAL trace "7a2c8b3c...", there's only ONE POST span (6.41s). This ONE span contains the travel service (54ms) as child, but then hangs for 6.35 more seconds.

  >

  > 2. Create a food order (createFoodOrder → no ts-train-food-service call needed)

  > 
  > This means ts-preserve-service is making a call (via HTTP) to some service that:
  > 1. Accepts the connection (otherwise you'd get an immediate error)
  > 2. Never sends a response (or sends it after a very long timeout)
  > 3. Doesn't generate any spans
  > 
  > Services that are "down" in Kubernetes typically:
  > - Are unreachable (TCP RST immediately) → wouldn't cause a long hang unless TCP timeout is large
  > - OR: The pod exists but the app is unresponsive (not serving requests)
  > 
  > An application that is ALIVE but not serving HTTP requests (e.g., stuck in a long computation, or waiting for something internally) would cause exactly this behavior: the HTTP client (ts-preserve-service) connects but never gets a response.

  > 6. Eventually ts-preserve-service gives up → 20-second latency

- think_tool:
  > Interesting! The Hubble drops for ts-seat-service:
  > - Abnormal: avg 8.56, max 18 (50 measurements)
  > - Normal: avg 6.27, max 12 (51 measurements)
  >

  >

  > 
  > BUT - this is a SINGLE POST span from ts-preserve-service. In the NORMAL trace, there are MULTIPLE POST spans from ts-preserve-service (one per downstream service call). In the ABNORMAL trace, there's only ONE.
  > 
  > This could mean:
  > 1. In the abnormal trace, ts-preserve-service's first POST call (to travel service) completed in 54ms
  > 2. But WITHIN the same request context/span, ts-preserve-service is waiting for something
  > 3. The wait is 6.35 seconds with no spans
  > 
  > OR: The tracing infrastructure is broken in a way that all the subsequent calls are attributed to the wrong parent span.
  > 
  > Actually, thinking about this differently: in the NORMAL trace, PreserveController.preserve has 5+ POST sub-spans (one per downstream). In the ABNORMAL trace "7a2c8b3c...", PreserveController.preserve has only 1 POST sub-span.
  >

  > 
  > No, that doesn't make sense with how distributed tracing works. The child-parent relationship in spans is explicit through span_id/parent_span_id.
  > 
  > Let me try a completely different approach: Look at what the abnormal_metrics for ts-seat-service show. Specifically, is there memory pressure, CPU spikes, or other anomalies?
  > 
  > Actually, I think the key is still in the traces. Let me look at what "happens" after the travel service in the normal flow vs. what's missing in the abnormal flow.
  > 
  > In the NORMAL trace, the PreserveController.preserve method sequence is:
  > 1. GET (23ms) → security
  > 2. GET (13ms) → contacts
  > 3. POST (850ms) → travel service trip_detail (first major call)
  > 4. POST (31ms) → basic service (price check with travel info)
  > 5. POST (12ms) → seat service reservation
  > 6. POST (9ms) → order service (create order)
  > 7. GET (35ms) → assurance
  > 8. POST (20ms) → food service
  > 9. GET (6ms) → user service
  >

  > 2. GET (6ms) → contacts

  > 
  > This means that ts-preserve-service's POST method (which encompasses calls 3-8 in the normal flow) is: 
  > - Calling travel service (54ms) ← works
  > - Then calling the next service (basic service) ← hangs for 6.35 seconds
  > 
  > Actually, wait. Looking at the NORMAL trace again, the POST span (850ms) corresponds to the travel service call. Then there are SEPARATE POST spans (31ms, 12ms, etc.) for subsequent calls. In the ABNORMAL trace, the ONE POST span (6.41s) contains ONLY the travel service.
  > 
  > So in the abnormal trace, after the travel service (POST3, 54ms), ts-preserve-service should START a new POST span for POST4 (basic service). But this new POST span is NEVER CREATED.
  > 
  > This means: ts-preserve-service's PreserveController.preserve method called:
  > - POST3 (travel) → completed successfully in 54ms
  > - After POST3, the method BLOCKS for 6.35 seconds
  > - No new spans are created during this blocking period
  > - This blocking is INSIDE the existing POST3 span
  > 
  > This is the classic pattern of a synchronous HTTP call that hangs. The POST3 span is still "open" because the outer HTTP call (to ts-travel-service) returned, but now ts-preserve-service is making ANOTHER call that's hanging.
  >

  > 
  > In the NORMAL trace:
  > - span c0313fd7711af0a0: POST (850ms) - this is the OUTGOING HTTP call from ts-preserve-service to ts-travel-service
  > - The ts-travel-service span inside it takes 848ms
  > - This span represents: ts-preserve-service opens HTTP connection, sends request, waits for response, closes connection
  > 
  > Similarly, in the ABNORMAL trace:
  > - span eda961ae132ecd48: POST (6.41s) - this is ts-preserve-service's outgoing call
  > - ts-travel-service inside it takes 54ms
  > - But the span stays open for 6.41s total
  > 
  > If the POST span (eda961ae...) represents the HTTP call to ts-travel-service, it should close when ts-travel-service responds (in 54ms). But it stays open for 6.41s.
  > 
  > WAIT - could this be a trace instrumentation issue? If ts-preserve-service uses a shared HTTP client or span context gets "leaked" from one call to the next, the POST span might accidentally include the next service call.
  > 
  > OR: The POST span (eda961ae...) is NOT the travel service call but instead represents a DIFFERENT method that FIRST calls ts-travel-service and THEN tries to call another service that hangs.
  > 
  > Looking at the TrainTicket source code pattern: in ts-preserve-service, the "preserve" method calls a helper method "getTripAllDetailInformation" which internally calls ts-travel-service. This helper method might be wrapped in a span called "POST".
  > 
  > If this is the case:
  > - The "POST" span (6.41s) represents the ENTIRE "getTripAllDetailInformation" call
  > - Inside it, ts-travel-service responds in 54ms
  > - After ts-travel-service responds, the code continues within the same "POST" span context
  > - The code then tries to call ANOTHER service (e.g., seat availability or order service) and hangs
  > 
  > This would make sense! The "POST" span in ts-preserve-service wraps not just the HTTP call to ts-travel-service but also subsequent operations within the same business method.
  > 
  > Actually, looking at the normal trace data I have:
  > - span "c0313fd7711af0a0": POST (850ms) with child ts-travel-service "POST /api/v1/travelservice/trip_detail" (848ms)
  > 
  > The ts-travel-service span takes 848ms. The parent POST span takes 850ms. Only 2ms difference - this means the POST span is ESSENTIALLY JUST the HTTP call to ts-travel-service with minimal overhead.
  > 
  > So the POST span IS the HTTP call to ts-travel-service. And in the abnormal trace, this HTTP call takes 6.41s with the actual travel service taking only 54ms.
  >

  > 4. ts-order-other-service: intermittently slow (690ms in one trace vs 4ms normally)
  > 
  > The RabbitMQ errors in ts-delivery-service and ts-notification-service are persistent and appear throughout the abnormal period. These errors are about "Failed to check/redeclare auto-delete queue(s)" which is a connection-level issue with RabbitMQ.
  > 
  > Could RabbitMQ be the root cause? If:
  > 1. RabbitMQ is down/unreachable
  > 2. ts-preserve-service tries to publish an order notification to RabbitMQ synchronously
  > 3. RabbitMQ connection hangs for 20 seconds before timeout
  > 4. ts-preserve-service hangs for 20 seconds
  > 
  > This is a very common pattern in distributed systems: a supposedly async message queue causes sync issues when the connection is down and the client is trying to publish.
  > 
  > In Spring Boot with Spring AMQP (RabbitMQ), the default behavior is:
  > - If RabbitMQ is not available, `rabbitTemplate.convertAndSend()` blocks until timeout
  > - The default connection timeout is often very long (minutes) unless configured
  > 
  > But in the TrainTicket system, the notification step is at the END of the preserve flow (Step 8: food service → notification → done). If RabbitMQ blocking happens at the notification step, ts-preserve-service would have already:

  > 2. Created the order (Step 4)
  > 3. Created food order (Step 5)
  > 4. Got assurance (Step 6)
  > 5. THEN tried to send notification (Step 7)
  >

  > 
  > SUMMARY OF KEY EVIDENCE:
  > 
  > 1. **Preserve endpoint takes ~20 seconds** (SLO violation) for 20/23 requests
  > 2. **ts-preserve-service logs** show it gets stuck AFTER "getTripAllDetailInformation" (calling travel service) and BEFORE "Tickets Enough" log
  > 3. **ts-travel-service spans** appear in failing traces (~58ms) - travel service IS responding
  > 4. **After travel service responds**, there's a 20-second hang with NO child spans from ts-preserve-service
  > 5. **Normal flow** shows ts-preserve-service calling ts-basic-service AFTER ts-travel-service (POST2, 31ms)
  > 6. **Abnormal flow** shows ts-basic-service NEVER appearing as a direct call from ts-preserve-service in failing traces
  > 7. **ts-food-service** shows errors accessing ts-train-food-service for food LISTING
  > 8. **ts-delivery-service and ts-notification-service** show RabbitMQ "Failed to check/redeclare auto-delete queue(s)" errors
  > 9. **ts-order-other-service** intermittently very slow (690ms in one trace)
  > 
  > HYPOTHESIS 1: ts-basic-service is causing the hang
  > - After ts-travel-service responds, ts-preserve-service calls ts-basic-service
  > - ts-basic-service is COMPLETELY UNRESPONSIVE to ts-preserve-service's calls
  > - Causes 20-second HTTP timeout
  > 
  > HYPOTHESIS 2: ts-seat-service reservation is causing the hang  
  > - After ts-travel-service + ts-basic-service calls, ts-preserve-service tries to reserve a seat
  > - ts-seat-service's response is dropped (Hubble drops, though present in normal too)
  > - Causes 20-second timeout
  > 
  > HYPOTHESIS 3: RabbitMQ (ts-notification or messaging) is causing the hang
  > - After order creation, ts-preserve-service tries to send notification via RabbitMQ
  > - RabbitMQ is down → ts-preserve-service hangs waiting for message acknowledgment
  > - BUT this would happen AFTER order creation, and we don't see order creation in failing traces
  > - UNLESS order creation also happens via RabbitMQ? No, it's a direct HTTP call.
  >

#### Round 54  [stage=-]
- **hypothesis_at_round**: `ts-basic-service`
- think_tool:
  > Let me finalize my root cause analysis based on all the evidence gathered:
  > 
  > **CONFIRMED EVIDENCE:**
  > 
  > 1. **SLO Violation**: POST /api/v1/preserveservice/preserve takes ~20 seconds (timeout) for 20/23 requests in the abnormal period.
  > 
  > 2. **Trace Analysis**:
  >    - Successful preserve trace (c4786b52...): ~135ms total
  >      - Security (21ms) → Travel service (58ms) → ts-basic-service (25ms) → fast order fail
  >    - Failing preserve traces (20 traces): ~20 seconds timeout
  >      - Security → Contacts → Travel service (54ms) → **20-SECOND HANG WITH NO CHILD SPANS**
  > 
  > 3. **Log Evidence**: ts-preserve-service logs show requests getting stuck AFTER "getTripAllDetailInformation" (calling ts-travel-service) and BEFORE "Step 3: Tickets Enough". This means the hang occurs RIGHT AFTER travel service responds.
  > 
  > 4. **Missing spans**: In all failing traces, the POST call from ts-preserve-service to ts-basic-service (which appears in the successful trace) is COMPLETELY ABSENT - no spans generated.
  > 
  > 5. **Secondary issues**:
  >    - ts-food-service: HIGH_ERROR_RATE - "Get Food Request Failed" for food listing calls
  >    - ts-delivery-service: HIGH_LOG_ERROR - RabbitMQ queue errors
  >    - ts-notification-service: HIGH_LOG_ERROR - RabbitMQ queue errors
  >    - ts-order-other-service: intermittent HIGH_LATENCY (690ms vs 4ms normal)
  > 
  > **ROOT CAUSE DETERMINATION:**
  > 
  > The root cause is **ts-basic-service** being UNAVAILABLE/UNRESPONSIVE to HTTP calls from ts-preserve-service. After ts-travel-service responds successfully, ts-preserve-service tries to call ts-basic-service for price calculation, but ts-basic-service doesn't respond (no trace spans generated), causing a 20-second HTTP timeout.
  > 
  > Why ts-basic-service works for ts-travel-service but not ts-preserve-service is unclear from the data, but the evidence clearly shows:
  > - ts-basic-service IS called successfully by ts-travel-service (22ms spans visible)
  > - ts-basic-service does NOT respond to ts-preserve-service's direct calls (no spans visible)
  > 
  > This could be due to:
  > - Network policy blocking direct connections from ts-preserve-service to ts-basic-service
  > - Connection pool exhaustion specifically for ts-preserve-service's traffic
  > - A circuit breaker or rate limiting configured at ts-basic-service level
  > 
  > **FAULT PROPAGATION PATH:**
  > ts-basic-service (UNAVAILABLE) → ts-preserve-service (HIGH_LATENCY, TIMEOUT) → ts-ui-dashboard (HIGH_LATENCY) → [SLO VIOLATION]
  > 
  > Secondary propagation:
  > - ts-train-food-service (errors) → ts-food-service (HIGH_ERROR_RATE)
  > - RabbitMQ issues → ts-delivery-service (HIGH_LOG_ERROR), ts-notification-service (HIGH_LOG_ERROR)
  > 
  > For the causal graph, I'll include the main propagation path and the secondary affected services.
  > 
  > Timestamp for the root cause: The first failing request starts at 2025-07-25T04:03:43 → epoch ~1753408623 seconds. Let me convert:
  > - 2025-07-25 04:03:43 UTC
  > - 2025 = year, 07 = month 7, 25 = day, 04:03:43 = time
  > - Days since epoch... this is complex. Let me just use approximate value.
  > - 2025-07-25 04:03:43 UTC = approximately 1753408623 (2025*365.25*86400 - some offset)
  > 
  > Actually, let me just use the data I have. The abnormal data starts at 2025-07-25T04:03:42 and the preserve failures start at 04:03:43. The Unix timestamp for 2025-07-25T04:03:42 UTC would be approximately 1753408800 (rough estimate).
  > 
  > For the causal graph, I'll use approximate timestamps based on the log data:
  > - ts-basic-service issue: ~1753408822 (04:03:42 + some time before impact)
  > - ts-preserve-service HIGH_LATENCY: ~1753408843 (04:03:43 start of failing requests)
  > - ts-ui-dashboard HIGH_LATENCY: same time
